 </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="right"><B>NEWS RELEASE </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>ARTHUR J. GALLAGHER&nbsp;&amp; CO. ANNOUNCES </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>FOURTH QUARTER AND FULL YEAR 2021 FINANCIAL RESULTS </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">ROLLING MEADOWS, IL, January&nbsp;27, 2022 &#151; Arthur J. Gallagher&nbsp;&amp; Co. (NYSE: AJG) today reported its financial results for the quarter and full
year ended December&nbsp;31, 2021. Management will host a webcast conference call to discuss these results on Thursday, January&nbsp;27, 2022 at 5:15 p.m. ET/4:15 p.m. CT. To listen to the call, and for printer-friendly formats of this release and
the &#147;Supplemental Quarterly Data&#148; and &#147;CFO Commentary,&#148; which may also be referenced during the call, please visit <U>ajg.com/IR</U>. These documents contain both GAAP and non-GAAP measures. Investors and other users of this
information should read carefully the section entitled &#147;Information Regarding Non-GAAP Measures&#148; beginning on page&nbsp;10. </P>

</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We delivered an outstanding fourth quarter, wrapping up another excellent year of financial
performance!&#148; said J. Patrick Gallagher, Jr., Chairman, President and CEO. &#147;During the quarter, our core brokerage and risk management segments combined to post 18% growth in revenue, of which 11% was organic revenue growth; net earnings
growth of 11%; and adjusted EBITDAC growth of 17%. We completed 18 new tuck-in mergers and our newly acquired reinsurance operations had a strong December. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;Overall, the P/C renewal premium increases we saw during the quarter were consistent with the first three quarters of 2021. P/C rates continued to move
higher across nearly all geographies and lines of coverage, insured exposure unit changes were positive, and inflation is at levels not seen for several decades. For the third straight quarter we benefited from positive policy endorsements and other
mid-term policy adjustments, indicating a rebound in the underlying economic health of our clients, notwithstanding the late-year surge in COVID-19 cases. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;Within our benefits and HR consulting business we saw rising covered lives and strong demand for special project work. And in our risk management and
claims paying unit, Gallagher Bassett, we had an excellent finish to the year fueled by new business wins and claim count increases. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;I am extremely
pleased with how our businesses performed during 2021 and that our 39,000 colleagues continue to deliver the very best insurance and risk management advice to clients and prospects, day-in and day-out. We have terrific momentum, which makes me
bullish about our prospects in 2022 and beyond!&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Summary of Financial Results - Year Ended December&nbsp;31, </B></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">*</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2021, the pretax impact of the Brokerage segment adjustments totals
$159.2&nbsp;million, with a corresponding adjustment to the provision for income taxes of $32.7&nbsp;million relating to these items. For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2021, the pretax impact of the Risk Management segment adjustments totals
$10.6&nbsp;million, with a corresponding adjustment to the provision for income taxes of $2.6&nbsp;million relating to these items. The pretax impact of the Corporate segment adjustments totals $73.6&nbsp;million, with a corresponding adjustment to
the benefit for income taxes of $(20.7)&nbsp;million relating to these items and the other tax items noted on pages&nbsp;8 and 9. A detailed reconciliation of the 2021 and 2020 provision (benefit) for income taxes is shown on pages&nbsp;14 and 15.
</P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Acquisition of the Willis Towers Watson Treaty Reinsurance Brokerage Operations </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On December&nbsp;1, 2021, we acquired substantially all of the Willis Towers Watson treaty reinsurance brokerage operations for an initial gross consideration
of $3.25&nbsp;billion, and potential additional consideration of $750&nbsp;million subject to certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">third-year</FONT> revenue targets.&nbsp;There are twelve remaining international operations with deferred closings
that comprise approximately $180&nbsp;million of the initial purchase consideration that are subject to local regulatory approval and are expected to close in the first and second quarters of 2022. We funded the transaction using cash on hand,
including $1.4&nbsp;billion of net cash raised in our May&nbsp;17, 2021 follow-on common stock offering, $850&nbsp;million of net cash borrowed in our May&nbsp;20, 2021 30-year senior note issuance, $750&nbsp;million of net cash borrowed in our
November&nbsp;9, 2021 10-year ($400&nbsp;million) and 30-year ($350&nbsp;million) senior note issuances and short-term borrowings. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Impact of COVID-19
Pandemic Recovery </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Relative to fourth quarter 2020, during fourth quarter 2021: </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Nearly all of our Brokerage segment operations&#146; revenues benefited from our clients&#146; improving business
conditions, which increases insured exposure units (i.e., insured values, payrolls, employees, miles driven, gross receipts, etc.) and covered lives, </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Our Risk Management segment operations&#146; revenues benefited from our clients&#146; improving business
conditions, which increases new arising workers&#146; compensation and general liability claims, and </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Our clean energy investments benefited from higher electricity production due to increased demand for electricity
from improving business conditions, somewhat offset by the sunset of our 2011-era plants in November and December of 2021. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">If economic
conditions continue to improve, we believe we may continue to see favorable revenue benefits in our Brokerage and Risk Management segments in the first quarter of 2022 relative to the same quarter in 2021. However, if the economic recovery slows,
due to the Omicron variant or other factors, we could see less revenue benefits than we experienced in the second, third and fourth quarters of 2021. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the second, third and fourth quarters of 2020 and first quarter of 2021, we realized significant expense savings (totaling approximately
$60&nbsp;million to $75&nbsp;million per quarter relative to the prior year same quarters, adjusted for pro forma full-quarter costs related to acquisitions) as a result of reduced travel, entertainment and advertising expenses, reduced costs from
lower employee medical plan utilization, a reduction in workforce, wage controls, and reduced use of external consultants. During the second, third and fourth quarters of 2021, as we increased our business activities relative to the second, third
and fourth quarters of 2020, we experienced increases in travel and entertainment, full restoration of advertising and more normalized usage of our employee medical plan, resumption of annual support-layer wage increases, increased use of external
consultants, further investment in support of our hybrid employee environment, continued investment in cyber security and an increase in incentive compensation. These incremental costs totaled approximately $15&nbsp;million, $25&nbsp;million and
$30&nbsp;million in our Brokerage segment relative to the second, third and fourth quarters of 2020, respectively. Looking forward to 2022, we believe we will see incrementally higher Brokerage segment costs relative to 2021, and if the pace of
economic recovery accelerates beyond our expectations, we could see expense increases higher than our current estimates. </P>

<TD WIDTH="2%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">*</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Reported fourth quarter 2021 compensation ratio was 2.4 pts lower than fourth quarter 2020. Adjusted fourth
quarter 2021 compensation ratio was 2.1 pts lower than fourth quarter 2020. Approximately one-third of the decrease in the ratio is due to workforce adjustment actions taken in 2020, approximately one-third is due to lesser employee benefit plan
costs and the remainder is the net impact of performance based compensation, partially offset by the resumption of merit wage increases. On a reported basis, the ratio was further impacted by differences in non-GAAP adjustments to revenue,
principally gains/losses from divestitures, and changes in compensation expense related to integration costs, workforce related charges and acquisition related adjustments between the periods. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

fourth quarter 2021 compensation ratio was 0.9&nbsp;pts lower than fourth quarter 2020. These ratios were primarily impacted by continued compensation savings in fourth quarter 2021 due to the 2020 workforce reduction actions and the phasing of

fourth quarter 2021 operating ratio was 1.5&nbsp;pts higher than fourth quarter 2020. These ratios were primarily impacted by modest incremental costs associated with the pandemic recovery as noted on page&nbsp;3 and increased professional fees

$8.7&nbsp;million in 2021 and $9.1&nbsp;million in 2020. Pretax losses for the years ended December&nbsp;31, are presented net of amounts attributable to noncontrolling interests of $39.8&nbsp;million in 2021 and $34.4&nbsp;million in 2020.

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(2)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Gallagher incurred transaction-related costs, which include legal, consulting, employee compensation and other
professional fees associated with due diligence and integration for its (a)&nbsp;acquisition of the Willis Towers Watson treaty reinsurance brokerage operations; and (b)&nbsp;the previous terminated agreement to acquire certain Willis Towers Watson
reinsurance and other brokerage operations. In connection with (b), in third quarter 2021, Gallagher redeemed $650&nbsp;million of 2031 Senior Notes and incurred a loss of $16.2 million related to the on early extinguishment of such debt.
</P></TD></TR></TABLE>

<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(3)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">In fourth quarter 2021, Gallagher incurred (a)&nbsp;additional U.K. and U.S. income tax expense related to the
non-deductibility of acquisition related adjustments made in the quarter, (b)&nbsp;costs related to a legal settlement and (c)&nbsp;income tax adjustments as we filed our 2020 tax returns in the fourth quarter and finalized our 2021 income tax
provisions within the U.S. and foreign jurisdictions where we operate. In third quarter 2021, Gallagher incurred additional U.K. income tax expense related to the non-deductibility of acquisition related adjustments made in that quarter. In second
quarter 2021, the U.K. government enacted tax legislation that increases the corporate income tax rate from 19% to 25% effective in 2023, in which Gallagher incurred additional income tax expense during 2021 to adjust certain deferred income tax
liabilities to the higher income tax rate. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(4)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Corporate pretax loss includes a net unrealized foreign exchange remeasurement gain of $1.5&nbsp;million in
fourth quarter 2021 and a net unrealized foreign exchange remeasurement loss of $5.0&nbsp;million in fourth quarter 2020. Corporate pretax loss includes a net unrealized foreign exchange remeasurement loss of $0.7&nbsp;million in the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2021 and a net unrealized foreign exchange remeasurement loss of $0.3&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2020. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Interest and banking costs and debt </B>- At December&nbsp;31, 2021, Gallagher had $1,600.0&nbsp;million of borrowings from public debt,
$4,448.0&nbsp;million of borrowings from private placements and $45.0&nbsp;million of short-term borrowings under its line of credit facility. In addition, Gallagher had $228.4&nbsp;million outstanding under a revolving loan facility that provides
funding for premium finance receivables, which are fully collateralized by the underlying premiums held by insurance carriers, and as such are excluded from our debt covenant computations. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Clean energy -</B> Consists of the operating results related to our investments in clean coal production plants and royalty income from clean coal licenses
related to Chem-Mod LLC. Additional information regarding these results is available in the &#147;CFO Commentary&#148; at <U>ajg.com/IR</U>. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Acquisition costs -</B> Consists mostly of external professional fees and other due diligence costs related to acquisitions. On occasion, Gallagher enters
into forward currency hedges for the purchase price of committed, but not yet funded, acquisitions with funding requirements in currencies other than the U.S. dollar. The gains or losses, if any, associated with these hedge transactions is also
included. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Corporate </B>- Consists of overhead allocations mostly related to corporate staff compensation, other corporate level activities, and net
unrealized foreign exchange remeasurement. In addition, includes the tax expense related to partial taxation of foreign earnings, nondeductible executive compensation and entertainment expenses and the tax benefit from vesting of employee equity
awards. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Income Taxes </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gallagher allocates the
provision for income taxes to its Brokerage and Risk Management segments using the local country statutory rates. Gallagher&#146;s consolidated effective tax rate for the quarters ended December&nbsp;31, 2021 and 2020 was (7.0)% and (14.5)%,
respectively, which was lower than the statutory rate due to the production of IRC Section&nbsp;45 clean energy tax credits. In third quarter 2020, Gallagher increased its estimated U.K. effective income tax rate from 17.5% to 19%. In second quarter
2021, the U.K. government enacted tax legislation that increases the corporate income tax rate from 19% to 25% effective in 2023. Gallagher incurred additional income tax expense during 2021 to adjust certain deferred income tax liabilities to the
higher income tax rate. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Webcast Conference Call </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gallagher will host a webcast conference call on Thursday, January&nbsp;27, 2022 at 5:15 p.m. ET/4:15 p.m. CT. To listen to this call, please go to
<U>ajg.com/IR</U>. The call will be available for replay at such website for at least 90 days. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About Arthur J. Gallagher&nbsp;&amp; Co. </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Arthur J. Gallagher&nbsp;&amp; Co., an international insurance brokerage and risk management services firm, is headquartered in Rolling Meadows, Illinois, has
operations in 68 countries and offers client-service capabilities in more than 150 countries around the world through a network of correspondent brokers and consultants. </P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Information Regarding Non-GAAP Measures </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In addition to
reporting financial results in accordance with GAAP, this press release provides information regarding EBITDAC, EBITDAC margin, adjusted EBITDAC, adjusted EBITDAC margin, diluted net earnings per share, as adjusted (adjusted EPS), adjusted revenue,
adjusted compensation and operating expenses, adjusted compensation expense ratio, adjusted operating expense ratio and organic revenue.&nbsp;These measures are not in accordance with, or an alternative to, the GAAP information provided in this
press release.&nbsp;Gallagher&#146;s management believes that these presentations provide useful information to management, analysts and investors regarding financial and business trends relating to Gallagher&#146;s results of operations and
financial condition or because they provide investors with measures that our chief operating decision maker uses when reviewing the company&#146;s performance. See further below for definitions and additional reasons each of these measures is useful
to investors. Gallagher&#146;s industry peers may provide similar supplemental non-GAAP information with respect to one or more of these measures, although they may not use the same or comparable terminology and may not make identical
adjustments.&nbsp;The non-GAAP information provided by Gallagher should be used in addition to, but not as a substitute for, the GAAP information provided.&nbsp;As disclosed in its most recent Proxy Statement, Gallagher makes determinations
regarding certain elements of executive officer incentive compensation, performance share awards and annual cash incentive awards, partly on the basis of measures related to adjusted EBITDAC. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Adjusted Non-GAAP presentation</B> - Gallagher believes that the adjusted non-GAAP presentations of the current and prior period information presented in
this earnings release provide stockholders and other interested persons with useful information regarding certain financial metrics of Gallagher that may assist such persons in analyzing Gallagher&#146;s operating results as they develop a future
earnings outlook for Gallagher. The after-tax amounts related to the adjustments were computed using the normalized effective tax rate for each respective period. See pages&nbsp;14 and 15 for a reconciliation of the adjustments made to income taxes.

by adjusted revenues. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Non-GAAP Earnings Measures </B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>EBITDAC and EBITDAC margin </B>- EBITDAC is net earnings before interest, income taxes, depreciation,
amortization and the change in estimated acquisition earnout payables and EBITDAC margin is EBITDAC divided by total revenues (for the Brokerage segment) and revenues before reimbursements (for the Risk Management segment). These measures for the
Brokerage and Risk Management segments provide a meaningful representation of Gallagher&#146;s operating performance for the overall business and provide a meaningful way to measure its financial performance on an ongoing basis.
</P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Adjusted EBITDAC and Adjusted EBITDAC Margin </B>- Adjusted EBITDAC is EBITDAC adjusted to exclude net gains
losses on divestitures, acquisition integration costs, workforce related charges, lease termination related charges, acquisition related adjustments, transaction related costs, legal and income tax related costs, loss on extinguishment of debt and
the period-over-period impact of foreign currency translation, as applicable and Adjusted EBITDAC margin is Adjusted EBITDAC divided by total adjusted revenues (defined above). These measures for the Brokerage and Risk Management segments provide a
meaningful representation of Gallagher&#146;s operating performance, and are also presented to improve the comparability of our results between periods by eliminating the impact of the items that have a high degree of variability.
</P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Adjusted EPS and Adjusted Net Earnings </B>- Adjusted net earnings have been adjusted to exclude the after-tax
impact of net gains losses on divestitures, acquisition integration costs, the impact of foreign currency translation, workforce related charges, lease termination related charges, acquisition related adjustments, transaction related costs, legal
and income tax related costs, loss on extinguishment of debt and effective income tax rate impact, as applicable. Adjusted EPS is Adjusted Net Earnings divided by diluted weighted average shares outstanding. This measure provides a meaningful
representation of Gallagher&#146;s operating performance (and as such should not be used as a measure of Gallagher&#146;s liquidity), and for the overall business is also presented to improve the comparability of our results between periods by
eliminating the impact of the items that have a high degree of variability. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Organic Revenues (a non-GAAP measure)</B> - For the
Brokerage segment, organic change in base commission and fee revenues, supplemental revenues and contingent revenues exclude the first twelve months of such revenues generated from acquisitions and such revenues related to divested operations in
each year presented.&nbsp;These revenues are excluded from organic revenues in order to help interested persons analyze the revenue growth associated with the operations that were a part of Gallagher in both the current and prior periods.&nbsp;In
addition, organic change in base commission and fee revenues, supplemental revenues and contingent revenues excludes the period-over-period impact of foreign currency translation to improve the comparability of our results between periods by
eliminating the impact of the items that have a high degree of variability. For the Risk Management segment, organic change in fee revenues excludes the first twelve months of fee revenues generated from acquisitions in each year presented. In
addition, change in organic growth excludes the period-over-period impact of foreign currency translation to improve the comparability of our results between periods by eliminating the impact of the items that have a high degree of variability. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">These revenue items are excluded from organic revenues in order to determine a comparable, but non-GAAP, measurement of revenue growth that is associated with
the revenue sources that are expected to continue in the current year and beyond.&nbsp;Gallagher has historically viewed organic revenue growth as an important indicator when assessing and evaluating the performance of its Brokerage and Risk
Management segments.&nbsp;Gallagher also believes that using this non-GAAP measure allows readers of our financial statements to measure, analyze and compare the growth from its Brokerage and Risk Management segments in a meaningful and consistent
manner. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Reconciliation of Non-GAAP Information Presented to GAAP Measures</B> - This press release includes tabular reconciliations to the most
comparable GAAP measures, as follows: for EBITDAC (on pages&nbsp;12 and 13, for adjusted revenues, adjusted EBITDAC and adjusted diluted net earnings per share (on pages&nbsp;1 and 2), for organic revenue measures (on pages&nbsp;4 and 6,
respectively, for the Brokerage and Risk Management segments), for adjusted compensation and operating expenses and adjusted EBITDAC margin (on pages&nbsp;5, 6 and 7, respectively, for the Brokerage and Risk Management segments). </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">(11 of 15) </P>

</DIV></Center>

e.removeAttribute('id');a.parentNode.appendChild(e)}}
if(e)e.style.display='block';Show.LastAR=e};Show.hideAR=function(){Show.LastAR.style.display='none'};Show.toggleNext=function(a){var e=a;while(e.nodeName!='DIV')e=e.nextSibling;if(!e.style){}else if(!e.style.display){}else{var d,p_;if(e.style.display=='none'){d='block';p='-'}else{d='none';p='+'}
e.style.display=d;if(a.textContent){a.textContent=p+a.textContent.substring(1)}else{a.innerText=p+a.innerText.substring(1)}}}
